<h1 class="firstHeading mw-first-heading" id="firstHeading"><span class="mw-page-title-main">Drink</span></h1>
<div class="vector-body" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"><div class="flaggedrevs_short flaggedrevs_stable_synced plainlinks noprint" id="mw-fr-revisiontag"><div class="flaggedrevs_short_basic"><span class="flaggedrevs-icon oo-ui-widget oo-ui-widget-enabled oo-ui-iconElement-icon oo-ui-icon-articleSearch oo-ui-iconElement oo-ui-labelElement-invisible oo-ui-iconWidget" title="Changes must be reviewed before being displayed on this page."></span><span class="fr-toggle-arrow oo-ui-widget oo-ui-widget-enabled oo-ui-indicatorElement-indicator oo-ui-indicator-down oo-ui-indicatorElement oo-ui-labelElement-invisible oo-ui-indicatorWidget" id="mw-fr-revisiontoggle" title="show/hide details"></span></div>
<div id="mw-fr-revisiondetails-wrapper" style="position:relative;"><div class="flaggedrevs_short_details" id="mw-fr-revisiondetails" style="display:none">This is the <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Pending_changes" title="Wikipedia:Pending changes">latest accepted revision</a>, <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Special:Log&amp;type=review&amp;page=Drink">reviewed</a> on <i>6 October 2022</i>.</div>
</div>

<div class="mw-body-content mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Liquid intended for human consumption</div><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">For the act of consuming a drink, see <a href="/wiki/Drinking" title="Drinking">Drinking</a>. For drinks containing alcohol, see <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alcoholic_drink" title="Alcoholic drink">Alcoholic drink</a>. For the 1917 film, see <a href="/wiki/Drink_(film)" title="Drink (film)">Drink (film)</a>.</div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">"Beverage" redirects here. Not to be confused with <a href="/wiki/Beveridge" title="Beveridge">Beveridge</a>.</div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nice_Cup_of_Tea.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3072" decoding="async" height="195" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Nice_Cup_of_Tea.jpg/260px-Nice_Cup_of_Tea.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Nice_Cup_of_Tea.jpg/390px-Nice_Cup_of_Tea.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Nice_Cup_of_Tea.jpg/520px-Nice_Cup_of_Tea.jpg 2x" width="260"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nice_Cup_of_Tea.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Tea" title="Tea">Tea</a> is the second‑most‑consumed drink in the world, after <a href="/wiki/Water" title="Water">water</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>A <b>drink</b> or <b>beverage</b> is a <a href="/wiki/Liquid" title="Liquid">liquid</a> intended for <a href="/wiki/Human" title="Human">human</a> consumption. In addition to their basic function of satisfying <a href="/wiki/Thirst" title="Thirst">thirst</a>, drinks play important roles in human <a href="/wiki/Culture" title="Culture">culture</a>. Common types of drinks include plain <a href="/wiki/Drinking_water" title="Drinking water">drinking water</a>, <a href="/wiki/Milk" title="Milk">milk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Juice" title="Juice">juice</a>, <a href="/wiki/Smoothie" title="Smoothie">smoothies</a> and <a href="/wiki/Soft_drink" title="Soft drink">soft drinks</a>. Traditionally <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hot_beverage" title="Hot beverage">warm beverages</a> include <a href="/wiki/Coffee" title="Coffee">coffee</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tea" title="Tea">tea</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hot_chocolate" title="Hot chocolate">hot chocolate</a>. <a href="/wiki/Caffeinated_drink" title="Caffeinated drink">Caffeinated drinks</a> that contain the stimulant <a href="/wiki/Caffeine" title="Caffeine">caffeine</a> have a long history.
</p><p>In addition, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alcoholic_drink" title="Alcoholic drink">alcoholic drinks</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Wine" title="Wine">wine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beer" title="Beer">beer</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Liquor" title="Liquor">liquor</a>, which contain the drug <a href="/wiki/Ethanol" title="Ethanol">ethanol</a>, have been part of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Human_culture" title="Human culture">human culture</a> for more than 8,000 years. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Non-alcoholic_drinks" title="Non-alcoholic drinks">Non-alcoholic drinks</a> often signify drinks that would normally contain alcohol, such as <a href="/wiki/Beer" title="Beer">beer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wine" title="Wine">wine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cocktail" title="Cocktail">cocktails</a>, but are made with a sufficiently low concentration of <a href="/wiki/Alcohol_by_volume" title="Alcohol by volume">alcohol by volume</a>. The category includes drinks that have undergone an alcohol removal process such as <a href="/wiki/Low-alcohol_beer" title="Low-alcohol beer">non-alcoholic beers</a> and de-alcoholized wines.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Biology">Biology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Drink&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Biology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>When the human body becomes <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dehydrated" title="Dehydrated">dehydrated</a>, a person experiences <a href="/wiki/Thirst" title="Thirst">thirst</a>. This craving of fluids results in an instinctive <i>need to drink</i>. Thirst is regulated by the <a href="/wiki/Hypothalamus" title="Hypothalamus">hypothalamus</a> in response to subtle changes in the body's <a href="/wiki/Electrolyte" title="Electrolyte">electrolyte</a> levels, and also as a result of changes in the volume of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blood_circulation" title="Blood circulation">blood circulating</a>. The complete deprivation of drinks (that is, <a href="/wiki/Water" title="Water">water</a>) will result in <a href="/wiki/Death" title="Death">death</a> faster than the removal of any other substance besides <a href="/wiki/Oxygen" title="Oxygen">oxygen</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cheney_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cheney-1">[1]</a></sup> Water and <a href="/wiki/Milk" title="Milk">milk</a> have been basic drinks throughout history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cheney_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-Cheney-1">[1]</a></sup> As water is essential for life, it has also been the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Water-borne_illness" title="Water-borne illness">carrier of many diseases</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Liquid_Pleasure_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-Liquid_Pleasure-2">[2]</a></sup>
</p><p>As <a href="/wiki/Society" title="Society">society</a> developed, techniques were discovered to create <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alcoholic_drinks" title="Alcoholic drinks">alcoholic drinks</a> from the plants that were available in different areas. The earliest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Archaeological" title="Archaeological">archaeological</a> evidence of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wine_production" title="Wine production">wine production</a> yet found has been at sites in <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">Georgia</a> (<span title="circa">c.</span><span style="white-space:nowrap;"> 6000</span> BCE)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-independent8k_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-independent8k-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-archaeology96_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-archaeology96-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cultures_of_The_World_Georgia_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cultures_of_The_World_Georgia-5">[5]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a> (<span title="circa">c.</span><span style="white-space:nowrap;"> 5000</span> BCE).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-indie_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-indie-6">[6]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Beer" title="Beer">Beer</a> may have been known in <a href="/wiki/Neolithic_Europe" title="Neolithic Europe">Neolithic Europe</a> as far back as 3000 BCE,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> and was mainly brewed on a domestic scale.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> The invention of beer (and <a href="/wiki/Bread" title="Bread">bread</a>) has been argued to be responsible for humanity's ability to develop <a href="/wiki/Technology" title="Technology">technology</a> and build <a href="/wiki/Civilization" title="Civilization">civilization</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tea" title="Tea">Tea</a> likely originated in <a href="/wiki/Yunnan" title="Yunnan">Yunnan</a>, China, during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shang_Dynasty" title="Shang Dynasty">Shang Dynasty</a> (1500 BCE–1046 BCE) as a medicinal drink.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-storyoftea_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-storyoftea-12">[12]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Drink&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Baco,_por_Caravaggio.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2500" data-file-width="2194" decoding="async" height="251" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Baco%2C_por_Caravaggio.jpg/220px-Baco%2C_por_Caravaggio.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Baco%2C_por_Caravaggio.jpg/330px-Baco%2C_por_Caravaggio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Baco%2C_por_Caravaggio.jpg/440px-Baco%2C_por_Caravaggio.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Baco,_por_Caravaggio.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Caravaggio" title="Caravaggio">Caravaggio</a>'s interpretation of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bacchus" title="Bacchus">Bacchus</a></div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Drinking" title="Drinking">Drinking</a> has been a large part of socialising throughout the centuries. In <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">Ancient Greece</a>, a social gathering for the purpose of drinking was known as a <a href="/wiki/Symposium" title="Symposium">symposium</a>, where watered down wine would be drunk. The purpose of these gatherings could be anything from serious discussions to direct indulgence. In <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Ancient Rome</a>, a similar concept of a <i>convivium</i> took place regularly.
</p><p>Many early societies considered alcohol a gift from the gods,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Beverage_Book_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-Beverage_Book-13">[13]</a></sup> leading to the creation of gods such as <a href="/wiki/Dionysus" title="Dionysus">Dionysus</a>. Other religions forbid, discourage, or restrict the drinking of alcoholic drinks for various reasons. In <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_with_alcohol_prohibition" title="List of countries with alcohol prohibition">some regions</a> with a dominant religion the production, sale, and consumption of alcoholic drinks is forbidden to everybody, regardless of religion.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Toast_(honor)" title="Toast (honor)">Toasting</a> is a method of honouring a person or wishing good will by taking a drink.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Beverage_Book_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-Beverage_Book-13">[13]</a></sup> Another tradition is that of the <a href="/wiki/Loving_cup" title="Loving cup">loving cup</a>, at weddings or other celebrations such as sports victories a group will share a drink in a large receptacle, shared by everyone until empty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Beverage_Book_13-2"><a href="#cite_note-Beverage_Book-13">[13]</a></sup>
</p><p>In East Africa and Yemen, coffee was used in native religious ceremonies. As these ceremonies conflicted with the beliefs of the Christian church, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ethiopian_Church" title="Ethiopian Church">Ethiopian Church</a> banned the secular consumption of coffee until the reign of Emperor <a href="/wiki/Menelik_II" title="Menelik II">Menelik II</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> The drink was also banned in <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman</a> Turkey during the 17th century for political reasons<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hopkins2006_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-hopkins2006-15">[15]</a></sup> and was associated with rebellious political activities in Europe.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Production">Production</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Drink&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Production">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>A drink is a form of liquid which has been prepared for human consumption. The preparation can include a number of different steps, some prior to transport, others immediately prior to consumption.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Purification_of_water">Purification of water</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Drink&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Purification of water">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Water_purification" title="Water purification">Water purification</a></div>
<p>Water is the chief constituent in all drinks, and the primary ingredient in most. Water is purified prior to <a href="/wiki/Drinking_water" title="Drinking water">drinking</a>. Methods for purification include <a href="/wiki/Filtration" title="Filtration">filtration</a> and the addition of chemicals, such as <a href="/wiki/Water_chlorination" title="Water chlorination">chlorination</a>. The importance of purified water is highlighted by the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a>, who point out 94% of deaths from <a href="/wiki/Diarrhea" title="Diarrhea">diarrhea</a> – the third biggest cause of infectious death worldwide at 1.8 million annually – could be prevented by improving the quality of the victim's environment, particularly safe water.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pasteurisation">Pasteurisation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Drink&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Pasteurisation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pasteurisation" title="Pasteurisation">Pasteurisation</a> is the process of heating a liquid for a period of time at a specified temperature, then immediately cooling. The process reduces the growth of <a href="/wiki/Microorganism" title="Microorganism">microorganisms</a> within the liquid, thereby increasing the time before spoilage. It is primarily used on <a href="/wiki/Milk" title="Milk">milk</a>, which prior to pasteurisation is commonly infected with <a href="/wiki/Pathogen" title="Pathogen">pathogenic</a> bacteria and therefore is more likely than any other part of the common diet in the developed world to cause illness.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wilson_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-wilson-17">[17]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Juicing">Juicing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Drink&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Juicing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pressoir_epi.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1373" data-file-width="1506" decoding="async" height="201" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Pressoir_epi.jpg/220px-Pressoir_epi.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Pressoir_epi.jpg/330px-Pressoir_epi.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Pressoir_epi.jpg/440px-Pressoir_epi.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pressoir_epi.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>First developed in the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Basket_press" title="Basket press">basket presses</a> have a long history of use in <a href="/wiki/Winemaking" title="Winemaking">winemaking</a>.</div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Juice" title="Juice">Juice</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pressing_(wine)" title="Pressing (wine)">Pressing (wine)</a></div>
<p>The process of extracting <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fruit_juice" title="Fruit juice">juice from fruits</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vegetable_juice" title="Vegetable juice">vegetables</a> can take a number of forms. Simple crushing of most fruits will provide a significant amount of liquid, though a more intense pressure can be applied to get the maximum amount of juice from the fruit. Both crushing and pressing are processes used in the production of <a href="/wiki/Wine" title="Wine">wine</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Infusion">Infusion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Drink&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Infusion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Infusion" title="Infusion">Infusion</a> is the process of extracting flavours from plant material by allowing the material to remain suspended within water. This process is used in the production of <a href="/wiki/Tea" title="Tea">teas</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Herbal_teas" title="Herbal teas">herbal teas</a> and can be used to prepare <a href="/wiki/Coffee" title="Coffee">coffee</a> (when using a <a href="/wiki/French_press" title="French press">coffee press</a>).
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Percolation">Percolation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Drink&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Percolation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coffee_percolation" title="Coffee percolation">Coffee percolation</a></div>
<p>The name is derived from the word "<a href="/wiki/Percolation" title="Percolation">percolate</a>" which means <i>to cause (a solvent) to pass through a permeable substance especially for extracting a soluble constituent</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup>
In the case of coffee-brewing the solvent is water, the permeable substance is the coffee grounds, and the soluble constituents are the chemical compounds that give coffee its color, taste, aroma, and stimulating properties.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Carbonation">Carbonation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Drink&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Carbonation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Carbonation" title="Carbonation">Carbonation</a> is the process of dissolving <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide">carbon dioxide</a> into a liquid, such as water.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fermentation">Fermentation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Drink&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Fermentation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Fermentation" title="Fermentation">Fermentation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fermentation_in_winemaking" title="Fermentation in winemaking">Fermentation in winemaking</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Beer" title="Beer">Beer</a></div>
<p>Fermentation is a <a href="/wiki/Metabolism" title="Metabolism">metabolic</a> process that converts <a href="/wiki/Sugar" title="Sugar">sugar</a> to <a href="/wiki/Ethanol" title="Ethanol">ethanol</a>. Fermentation has been used by humans for the production of drinks since the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neolithic_age" title="Neolithic age">Neolithic age</a>. In <a href="/wiki/Winemaking" title="Winemaking">winemaking</a>, grape juice is combined with yeast in an <a href="/wiki/Hypoxia_(environmental)" title="Hypoxia (environmental)">anaerobic</a> environment to allow the fermentation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cox_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-cox-19">[19]</a></sup> The amount of sugar in the wine and the length of time given for fermentation determine the alcohol level and the <a href="/wiki/Sweetness_of_wine" title="Sweetness of wine">sweetness of the wine</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bird_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bird-20">[20]</a></sup>
</p><p>When <a href="/wiki/Brewing" title="Brewing">brewing</a> beer, there are four primary ingredients – water, grain, yeast and hops. The grain is encouraged to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Germinate" title="Germinate">germinate</a> by soaking and drying in heat, a process known as <a href="/wiki/Malting" title="Malting">malting</a>. It is then milled before soaking again to create the sugars needed for fermentation. This process is known as <a href="/wiki/Mashing" title="Mashing">mashing</a>. Hops are added for flavouring, then the yeast is added to the mixture (now called <a href="/wiki/Wort" title="Wort">wort</a>) to start the fermentation process.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-beer_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-beer-21">[21]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Distillation">Distillation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Drink&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Distillation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Distillation" title="Distillation">Distillation</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Distilled_beverage" title="Distilled beverage">Distilled beverage</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Liquor_Still_Frankfort_489226997.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1280" data-file-width="960" decoding="async" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Liquor_Still_Frankfort_489226997.jpg/170px-Liquor_Still_Frankfort_489226997.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Liquor_Still_Frankfort_489226997.jpg/255px-Liquor_Still_Frankfort_489226997.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Liquor_Still_Frankfort_489226997.jpg/340px-Liquor_Still_Frankfort_489226997.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Liquor_Still_Frankfort_489226997.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An old <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Whiskey" title="Whiskey">whiskey</a> <a href="/wiki/Still" title="Still">still</a></div></div></div>
<p>Distillation is a method of <a href="/wiki/Separation_process" title="Separation process">separating</a> <a href="/wiki/Mixture" title="Mixture">mixtures</a> based on differences in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Volatility_(physics)" title="Volatility (physics)">volatility</a> of components in a boiling liquid mixture. It is one of the methods used in the purification of water. It is also a method of producing spirits from milder alcoholic drinks.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mixing">Mixing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Drink&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Mixing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Cocktail" title="Cocktail">Cocktail</a></div>
<p>An <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alcoholic_drink" title="Alcoholic drink">alcoholic</a> <a href="/wiki/Mixed_drink" title="Mixed drink">mixed drink</a> that contains two or more ingredients is referred to as a cocktail. Cocktails were originally a mixture of spirits, sugar, water, and <a href="/wiki/Bitters" title="Bitters">bitters</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> The term is now often used for almost any mixed drink that contains alcohol, including mixers, mixed shots, etc.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Regan_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-Regan-23">[23]</a></sup> A cocktail today usually contains one or more kinds of spirit and one or more <a href="/wiki/Drink_mixer" title="Drink mixer">mixers</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Carbonated_water" title="Carbonated water">soda</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fruit_juice" title="Fruit juice">fruit juice</a>. Additional ingredients may be <a href="/wiki/Sugar" title="Sugar">sugar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Honey" title="Honey">honey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Milk" title="Milk">milk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cream" title="Cream">cream</a>, and various <a href="/wiki/Herb" title="Herb">herbs</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Type">Type</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Drink&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Type">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Non-alcoholic_drinks">Non-alcoholic drinks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Drink&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Non-alcoholic drinks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ice_water_with_lemon.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1280" data-file-width="960" decoding="async" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Ice_water_with_lemon.jpg/170px-Ice_water_with_lemon.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Ice_water_with_lemon.jpg/255px-Ice_water_with_lemon.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Ice_water_with_lemon.jpg/340px-Ice_water_with_lemon.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ice_water_with_lemon.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ice water with a slice of <a href="/wiki/Lemon" title="Lemon">lemon</a></div></div></div>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/Non-alcoholic_drink" title="Non-alcoholic drink">non-alcoholic drink</a> is one that contains little or no <a href="/wiki/Ethanol" title="Ethanol">alcohol</a>. This category includes <a href="/wiki/Low-alcohol_beer" title="Low-alcohol beer">low-alcohol beer</a>, non-alcoholic <a href="/wiki/Wine" title="Wine">wine</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Apple_cider" title="Apple cider">apple cider</a> if they contain a sufficiently low concentration of <a href="/wiki/Alcohol_by_volume" title="Alcohol by volume">alcohol by volume</a> (ABV). The exact definition of what is "non-alcoholic" and what is not depends on local laws: in the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, "alcohol-free beer" is under 0.05% ABV, "de-alcoholised beer" is under 0.5%, while "low-alcohol beer" can contain no more than 1.2% ABV.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> The term "soft drink" specifies the absence of alcohol in contrast to "hard drink" and "drink". The term "drink" is theoretically neutral, but often is used in a way that suggests alcoholic content. Drinks such as soda pop, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sparkling_water" title="Sparkling water">sparkling water</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iced_tea" title="Iced tea">iced tea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lemonade" title="Lemonade">lemonade</a>, <a href="/wiki/Root_beer" title="Root beer">root beer</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fruit_punch" title="Fruit punch">fruit punch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Milk" title="Milk">milk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hot_chocolate" title="Hot chocolate">hot chocolate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tea" title="Tea">tea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coffee" title="Coffee">coffee</a>, <a href="/wiki/Milkshake" title="Milkshake">milkshakes</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tap_water" title="Tap water">tap water</a> and <a href="/wiki/Energy_drink" title="Energy drink">energy drinks</a> are all soft drinks.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Water">Water</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Drink&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Water">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Drinking_water" title="Drinking water">Drinking water</a> and <a href="/wiki/Water_resources" title="Water resources">Water resources</a></div>
<p>Water is the world's most consumed drink,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Griffiths_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-Griffiths-26">[26]</a></sup> however, 97% of water on Earth is non-drinkable salt water.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USGS_dist_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-USGS_dist-27">[27]</a></sup> Fresh water is found in rivers, lakes, wetlands, groundwater, and frozen glaciers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> Less than 1% of the Earth's fresh water supplies are accessible through surface water and underground sources which are cost effective to retrieve.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup>
</p><p>In western cultures, water is often drunk cold.  In the Chinese culture, it is typically drunk hot.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Milk">Milk</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Drink&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Milk">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Milk" title="Milk">Milk</a> is regarded as one of the "original" drinks,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> milk is the primary source of nutrition for babies. In many cultures of the world, especially the Western world, humans continue to consume dairy milk beyond infancy, using the milk of other animals (especially <a href="/wiki/Cattle" title="Cattle">cattle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Goat_milk" title="Goat milk">goats</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sheep_milk" title="Sheep milk">sheep</a>) as a drink.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Carbonated_drinks">Carbonated drinks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Drink&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Carbonated drinks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Carbonation" title="Carbonation">Carbonation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Soft_drink" title="Soft drink">Soft drink</a></div>
<p>Carbonated drinks refer to drinks which have carbon dioxide dissolved into them. This can happen naturally through fermenting and in natural water spas or artificially by the dissolution of carbon dioxide under pressure. The first commercially available artificially carbonated drink is believed to have been produced by Thomas Henry in the late 1770s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup>
Cola, orange, various roots, ginger, and lemon/lime are commonly used to create non-alcoholic carbonated drinks; sugars and preservatives may be added later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SIVASANKAR_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-SIVASANKAR-33">[33]</a></sup>
</p><p>The most consumed carbonated soft drinks are produced by three major global brands: <a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola" title="Coca-Cola">Coca-Cola</a>, <a href="/wiki/PepsiCo" title="PepsiCo">PepsiCo</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Dr_Pepper_Snapple_Group" title="Dr Pepper Snapple Group">Dr Pepper Snapple Group</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Juice_and_plant_drinks">Juice and plant drinks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Drink&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Juice and plant drinks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Oranges_and_orange_juice.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2700" data-file-width="1772" decoding="async" height="259" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Oranges_and_orange_juice.jpg/170px-Oranges_and_orange_juice.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Oranges_and_orange_juice.jpg/255px-Oranges_and_orange_juice.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Oranges_and_orange_juice.jpg/340px-Oranges_and_orange_juice.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Oranges_and_orange_juice.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Orange_(fruit)" title="Orange (fruit)">Orange</a> <a href="/wiki/Juice" title="Juice">juice</a> is usually served cold</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Juice" title="Juice">Fruit juice</a> is a natural product that contains few or no additives. Citrus products such as <a href="/wiki/Orange_juice" title="Orange juice">orange juice</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tangerine" title="Tangerine">tangerine</a> juice are familiar breakfast drinks, while <a href="/wiki/Grapefruit_juice" title="Grapefruit juice">grapefruit juice</a>, pineapple, apple, grape, lime, and lemon juice are also common. <a href="/wiki/Coconut_water" title="Coconut water">Coconut water</a> is a highly nutritious and refreshing juice. Many kinds of berries are crushed; their juices are mixed with water and sometimes sweetened. Raspberry, blackberry and <a href="/wiki/Ribes" title="Ribes">currants</a> are popular juices drinks but the percentage of water also determines their nutritive value. Grape juice allowed to ferment produces <a href="/wiki/Wine" title="Wine">wine</a>.
</p><p>Fruits are highly perishable so the ability to extract juices and store them was of significant value. Some fruits are highly acidic and mixing them with water and sugars or honey was often necessary to make them palatable. Fruits can also be blended with ice and other ingredients to make a <a href="/wiki/Smoothie" title="Smoothie">smoothie</a>. Early storage of fruit juices was labor-intensive, requiring the crushing of the fruits and the mixing of the resulting pure juices with sugars before bottling.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Vegetable_juice" title="Vegetable juice">Vegetable juices</a> are usually served warm or cold. Different types of vegetables can be used to make vegetable juice such as <a href="/wiki/Carrot" title="Carrot">carrots</a>, tomatoes, <a href="/wiki/Cucumber" title="Cucumber">cucumbers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Celery" title="Celery">celery</a> and many more. Some vegetable juices are mixed with some fruit juice to make the vegetable juice taste better. Many popular vegetable juices, particularly ones with high tomato content, are high in sodium, and therefore consumption of them for health must be carefully considered. Some vegetable juices provide the same health benefits as whole vegetables in terms of reducing risks of <a href="/wiki/Cardiovascular_disease" title="Cardiovascular disease">cardiovascular disease</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cancer" title="Cancer">cancer</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Plant_milk" title="Plant milk">Plant milk</a> is a general term for any milk-like product that is derived from a plant source. The most common varieties internationally are <a href="/wiki/Soy_milk" title="Soy milk">soy milk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Almond_milk" title="Almond milk">almond milk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rice_milk" title="Rice milk">rice milk</a> and <a href="/wiki/Coconut_milk" title="Coconut milk">coconut milk</a>.
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sleep_drinks">Sleep drinks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Drink&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Sleep drinks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/Nightcap_(drink)" title="Nightcap (drink)">nightcap</a> is a drink taken shortly before bedtime to induce sleep. For example, a small <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alcoholic_drink" title="Alcoholic drink">alcoholic drink</a> or a cup of <a href="/wiki/Sleep_induction" title="Sleep induction">warm milk</a> can supposedly promote a good night's sleep. Today, most nightcaps and <a href="/wiki/Relaxation_drink" title="Relaxation drink">relaxation drinks</a> are generally non-alcoholic beverages containing calming ingredients. They are considered beverages which serve to relax a person. Unlike other calming beverages, such as <a href="/wiki/Tea" title="Tea">tea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Warm_milk" title="Warm milk">warm milk</a> or <a href="/wiki/Milk" title="Milk">milk</a> with <a href="/wiki/Honey" title="Honey">honey</a>; relaxation drinks almost universally contain more than one active ingredient. Relaxation drinks have been known to contain other natural ingredients and are usually free of <a href="/wiki/Caffeine" title="Caffeine">caffeine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alcohol_(drug)" title="Alcohol (drug)">alcohol</a> but some have claimed to contain <a href="/wiki/Cannabis_(drug)" title="Cannabis (drug)">marijuana</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Alcoholic_drinks">Alcoholic drinks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Drink&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Alcoholic drinks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alcoholic_drink" title="Alcoholic drink">Alcoholic drink</a></div>
<p>A drink is considered "alcoholic" if it contains <a href="/wiki/Ethanol" title="Ethanol">ethanol</a>, commonly known as <a href="/wiki/Alcohol_(drug)" title="Alcohol (drug)">alcohol</a> (although in <a href="/wiki/Chemistry" title="Chemistry">chemistry</a> the definition of "alcohol" includes many other compounds). <a href="/wiki/Beer" title="Beer">Beer</a> has been a part of human civilisation for around 8,000 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Beer">Beer</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Drink&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Beer">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Beer" title="Beer">Beer</a> is an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alcoholic_drink" title="Alcoholic drink">alcoholic drink</a> produced by the <a href="/wiki/Hydrolysis" title="Hydrolysis">saccharification</a> of <a href="/wiki/Starch" title="Starch">starch</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fermentation_(food)" title="Fermentation (food)">fermentation</a> of the resulting sugar. The starch and saccharification <a href="/wiki/Enzyme" title="Enzyme">enzymes</a> are often derived from malted cereal grains, most commonly <a href="/wiki/Malt" title="Malt">malted</a> barley and malted wheat.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barth_2014_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-Barth_2014-41">[41]</a></sup> Most beer is also flavoured with <a href="/wiki/Hops" title="Hops">hops</a>, which <a href="/wiki/Bittering_agent" title="Bittering agent">add bitterness</a> and act as a natural <a href="/wiki/Preservative" title="Preservative">preservative</a>, though other flavourings such as herbs or fruit may occasionally be included. The preparation of beer is called <a href="/wiki/Brewing" title="Brewing">brewing</a>. Beer is the world's most widely consumed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alcoholic_drink" title="Alcoholic drink">alcoholic drink</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> and is the third-most consumed drink overall, after <a href="/wiki/Drinking_water" title="Drinking water">water</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tea" title="Tea">tea</a>. It is said to have been discovered by goddess <a href="/wiki/Ninkasi" title="Ninkasi">Ninkasi</a> around 5300 BCE, when she accidentally discovered yeast after leaving grain in jars that were later rained upon and left for several days. Women have been the chief creators of beer throughout history due to its association with domesticity and it, throughout much of history, being brewed in the home for family consumption. Only in recent history have men begun to dabble in the field.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nelson_2005_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-Nelson_2005-44">[44]</a></sup> It is thought by some to be the oldest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fermented_drink" title="Fermented drink">fermented drink</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup>
</p><p>Some of humanity's earliest known writings refer to the production and distribution of beer: the <a href="/wiki/Code_of_Hammurabi" title="Code of Hammurabi">Code of Hammurabi</a> included laws regulating beer and beer parlours,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> and "The Hymn to <a href="/wiki/Ninkasi" title="Ninkasi">Ninkasi</a>", a prayer to the Mesopotamian goddess of beer, served as both a prayer and as a method of remembering the recipe for beer in a culture with few literate people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nin-kasi_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-Nin-kasi-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sumer_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-sumer-51">[51]</a></sup> Today, the brewing industry is a global business, consisting of several dominant <a href="/wiki/Multinational_corporation" title="Multinational corporation">multinational companies</a> and many thousands of smaller producers ranging from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brewpubs" title="Brewpubs">brewpubs</a> to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Regional_brewery" title="Regional brewery">regional breweries</a>.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Cider">Cider</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Drink&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Cider">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Cider" title="Cider">Cider</a> is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fermentation_(food)" title="Fermentation (food)">fermented</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alcoholic_drink" title="Alcoholic drink">alcoholic drink</a> made from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fruit_juice" title="Fruit juice">fruit juice</a>, most commonly and traditionally <a href="/wiki/Apple_juice" title="Apple juice">apple juice</a>, but also the juice of <a href="/wiki/Peach" title="Peach">peaches</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pear" title="Pear">pears</a> ("Perry" cider) or other fruit. Cider may be made from any variety of apple, but certain <a href="/wiki/Cultivar" title="Cultivar">cultivars</a> grown solely for use in cider are known as <a href="/wiki/Cider_apple" title="Cider apple">cider apples</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> has the highest per capita consumption of cider, as well as the largest cider-producing companies in the world,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cideruk_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-cideruk-53">[53]</a></sup> As of 2006<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Drink&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the U.K. produces 600 million litres of cider each year (130 million imperial gallons).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Wine">Wine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Drink&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Wine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1096954695/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .multiimageinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle .thumbcaption{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow>.thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner multiimageinner"
